  33. +1 Star - nice looking unit including stand. Materials on unit look and feel high quality though plastic. Mine doesn't creak unless gripped very tightly. Lighting/indicators are mostly gratuitous but do look nice and battery indicator is helpful. Carry sleeve and blade protector have been handy for extensive travel. No complaints about battery life after 1 year, I charge whenever not in use but for testing purposes have tried up to 3 days without noticeable battery loss. +1 Star - very easy to clean. Simply lift the 3 heads and run under warm water, leave open to dry while it charges. Shaver and even stand have drain holes. Thoughtfully designed. -1 Star - replacement blades. Ridiculous stock shortages, price, substitution of different and apparently lower quality blades (please look at the photos and reviews of replacement blades before buying this unit - search for RQ12+ and RQ12/62). The blades are often so expensive and of such questionable quality it's almost better to just buy a new shaver during a ~$90 Black Friday sale. As an owner who had hoped to invest in a long-lasting shaver requiring only a reasonable-cost blade replacement every 9-12 months, I feel disgust toward the cost and hassle of finding replacements. -2 Stars - mediocre shave quality. I bought this hoping for 1) a shave that was fast - one or two slow circular passes, 2) close/clean including hard-to-reach areas, and 3) quiet when others are sleeping. Instead, after a year of use I have consistently throughout the life of my first blades found this unit to fall short on all 3 categories. Requires multiple passes in different directions. I spend about 15+ minutes per day shaving, otherwise look stubbly. Even with the multiple directions the blades can move, the unit struggles to get under what I would describe as a straight, taut jawline and under-chin area. Also struggles with upper lip below nose (blade housing is too chunky to get stubble close to nose). The blades consistently cutme, especially around the edge of my jaw and under my chin. This happens regardless of pressing the blades to get a closer cut - it's not very close otherwise - or lightly grazing the skin without pressure. The first day of every week is a slightly closer and less mauling shave as if it catches longer hair better if I don't shave over a weekend - every subsequent day leaves me cut up yet still stubbly in areas. The unit is also very loud. You can hear it easily with two closed doors between you and the shaver and you cannot, for example, hear someone talking to you or \\"average volume\\" music playing. The unit was quieter for the first few weeks of use but is now as loud or louder than the various other units I've used over the years. Bottom line: slow, painful, loud, poor shave even on taut skin, high cost, awful replacement blade options. Not a good investment. Regret purchase given high price. Build quality may warrant some cost, but shaving performance I would place around $25-30 value. NOTES: I wash the unit after every shave. Owned about 1 year, still using original blades due to cost/quality concerns. Issues noted above have been consistent throughout life of blade except time to shave which has gotten longer over time. I do not use any shaving creams or lubricants, though have tried some shaving cream samples we had on hand (feels nicer but no change to closeness of shave or cuts).

  152. I’ve used Norelco razors for years. The 1250X is first one I’ve used that has the cutting heads mounted in a futuristic looking pod on top of the razor. It certainly looks sleek. But in this review I hope to explain why I think the sleek design of this razor has unfortunately been at the expense of functionality.<br /><br />Daily Cleaning: The traditional style Norelco razor contains three (3) cutting heads within a single holder. You’re supposed to clean the razor after each use to get rid of loose hair and/or shaving gel (if you use shaving gel).<br /><br />To rinse a traditional model Norelco all you have to do is press one tab and the shaving head flips up to expose the cutting heads. Simply hold the assembly under hot running water and you’re done. On the 1250X the three (3) cutting heads are contained within their own holder. This means that you must first open (and subsequently close) all three holders in order to expose the cutting heads for rinsing. It also means that you have to position each individual head under a running stream of hot water to clean them. This may not seem like such a big deal, but read on.<br /><br />Extensive Cleaning: After several uses all Norelco razors benefit from the blades being removed from the cutting combs for more extensive cleaning. On the traditional models all you have to do is easily remove a retainer and all three cutting heads can be popped out for cleaning. However, on the 1250X there are three metal holders (one for each cutting head) that must be opened individually to get to the blades. The metal holders can sometimes be a bit tricky to open. Again, this may not seem like such a big deal. But my point is that it’s less convenient to rinse and extensively clean the blades on the 1250X than it is on the traditional style Norelco razors.<br /><br />Note: Norelco offers more expensive models that include a “Jet Clean System” (not included with the 1250X). Essentially, it’s a base thatcontains a cleaning solution that automatically cleans your razor. I’ve never used one of these. Maybe they work great. But I really have no interest in using an automated cleaner that has to be refilled periodically with a special cleaning solution. I’ve always found that hot running water and some isopropyl alcohol in a spray bottle works just fine.<br /><br />Pop-up Trimmer: The pop-up trimmer on the 1250X is about ½” wide. On the traditional model Norelco the trimmer is almost 1” wide. I use the trimmer daily for my mustache and sideburns. Bottom Line: It’s easier and faster to get a straight line with a 1” wide trimmer versus one that’s about half the width.<br /><br />Charging Cord: On the traditional Norelco razor the charging cord plugs directly into the bottom of the razor (simple enough). On the 1250X the razor can only be charged by placing it in the stand. Personally, I find it easier and more practical to just plug the charging cord directly into the razor when it needs a charge. Why? Well, the stand just takes up room on the bathroom countertop. And if you’re traveling, it means you also have to bring along the stand (instead of just a small AC adapter) in order to charge your razor.<br /><br />Furthermore, I never charge my Norelco razor until the battery gets low and the light starts flashing to remind you it’s time for a charge. It seems to me that the stand only encourages you to put the razor back in the charger after each use. My personal experience with rechargeable batteries (including Lithium-Ion types) is that they last longer if you don’t charge them every day. There are varying opinions on how or how often Li-Ion batteries should be charged. But many sources suggest that daily charging may overcharge and/or otherwise shorten the life of the battery.<br /><br />Shave Quality: I’d be willing to put up with the additional expense and the little things that annoy me about this razor if it offered a superior shave. It doesn’t. Traditional Norelco razors costing less than half as much as the 1250X provide a shave that’s just as close and just as comfortable.<br /><br />So what do we have here? Well, the 1250X is certainly a cool and sleek looking razor (I believe that if there was a beauty contest for electric shavers, it just might win). And I like the fact that it’s made in the Netherlands (not China, like some of Norelco’s other models). And yes, it certainly shaves very well.<br /><br />But I can’t give this razor more than two stars because a traditional Norelco razor provides a shave that’s just as close and comfortable, has a better pop-up trimmer, is easier and faster to clean, doesn’t need a stand to take a charge, and costs less than half as much as the 1250X.

  447. I purchased my SensoTouch 3D during the last week of March 2013 and edited this review progressively over my first three weeks with it. I previously used a Mach3 on a daily basis. I have thick facial hair.<br /><br />Week 1-<br />I got a better shave than I could with a Mach3 from the very first time I used this shaver. I've used Norelco shavers before and have been disappointed with the results, but the SensoTouch was comfortable the whole way and got very, very close. It must be the design of the shaving head, which seems to catch more hairs at different angles. This ain't your daddy's Norelco.<br />The first shave did result in some neck irritation, but I found a couple of strategies to avoid it. First, I dust my face and neck with a little bit of baby powder. It's a simple way to reduce friction while shaving. I also had a tendency to shave in small, fast circles but it works better to make large, slow circles.<br />It works best for me to clean this shaver daily. I like that I can give it a quick rinse, and using the baby powder seems to keep it from getting clogged with hair.<br /><br />Week 2-<br />I got some vicious ingrown hairs around the corners of my mouth and chin this week. After buying a top-of-the-line electric razor, why did it suddenly tear up my face so badly? The reality is that making the transition from wet shaving with a cartridge razor to dry shaving with an electric is a totally different ballgame. You simply cannot apply pressure with this razor or you will hurt yourself. Further, once I've shaved an area of my face or neck it's best for me to just leave it and not come back. With proper technique, I don't have to do touch-ups. Finally, for me it works best to shave every day and to use a drying agent (talcum powder) on my face before shaving.<br />I'm very impressed by the battery. Two weeks on and I've still got two out of three bars.<br /><br />Week 3-<br />I decided to take the blades out of their housing for a more thorough cleaning with the included brush.   525. If you're like me and have spent more hours than you'd care to admit poring over Amazon reviews before buying an expensive electric shaver, you know that guys and faces and beards vary so much that one man's perfect shaver is another man's living hell. So I'll start by providing some context and moving on from there.<br /><br />I have extremely thick and tough whiskers compounded with an incredibly sensitive face that is easily damaged by shaving, so I can't shave every day. Even better, I'm a bit OCD so when I shave I can't stop until my face and neck are *smooth*. Fun! My specific needs, then, are:<br /><br />* Must shave my face smooth.<br />* Must not be too painful or rip my face up too much.<br />* Must be able to handle my fast-growing, adamantium stubble after two or three days.<br />* Must be a good wet shaver, because forget dry shaving.<br /><br />Things I don't care about:<br /><br />* Dry shaving. I won't dry shave so I can't comment on that.<br />* Battery life. Long battery life is a plus, but not a deal breaker for me. Happily the 1250X/46 has great battery life in my experience.<br />* Volume of noise. I don't care if it sounds like a lawn mower as long as it meets my above requirements. Happily again, though, this shaver is surprisingly quiet, which I know will be a plus for a lot of you.<br />* Speed. Given my requirements, shaving in ten minutes before dashing off to work simply isn't an option, or even physically possible, so I can't comment on how fast you can shave with this thing.<br />* Sideburn or other trimming. I have a separate trimmer I use and like for that. All I want this thing to do is handle my face.<br />* Self-cleaning systems. I can clean it myself. Those things are a racket so they can sell you cleaning supplies.<br />* Fancy displays. I just want to know how much charge is left.<br /><br />I had tried a few cheap (under $100 suggested retail) electric shavers over the years and had nothing but terrible experiences. I decided, out of desperation and pain with my various blades, to bite the bullet and shell out the bucks for a not-cheap electric shaver. I ended up getting the Panasonic ES-LA63 Wet/Dry and *loved* it. It was loud and didn't have great battery life, but it nailed all my actual requirements and made me insanely happy. Sadly, after just over a year or so it developed the LDC display problem and then a couple months after that crapped out entirely (you can see my review of the ES-LA63 here on Amazon, although you just got the important points in summary). After a few months of suffering through blade use again, I decided I had to spend the money and try a new electric.<br /><br />After another round of time consuming and obsessive research and review reading I bought this shaver, the 1250X/46. I was extremely reluctant to do so, because my past experiences with cheap rotary shavers had been the worst shaving experiences of my life. But I decided to give this one a shot specifically because I read a detailed review from a guy who had the tough-beard/wussy-face combo I deal with and who also only shaves every two or three days. As it happens, that dude was right and this shaver is great for me and meets all my requirements discussed above. My only caveat is that it gets 95% of my face as smooth or smoother than a blade, *but* there are a couple odd spots on my neck that it doesn't get completely smooth no matter how much I go over them. No big, I just hit those with my blade when I'm done and I'm good to go -- a small inconvenience for what I am getting overall, which is smooth and far less pain and skin irritation than with a blade or a cheap electric. Again, as mentioned above, I only use this thing wet and I take my time because speed is not a priority for me.<br /><br />If your situation sounds similar to mine, then I highly recommend this shaver. The only thing I can add is that I really liked the Frustration Free Packaging and wish more products came this way (especially mydaughter's toys -- cripes, what's with those stupid indestructible twist ties?!?). Anyway, recommended.daughter's toys -- cripes, what's with those stupid indestructible twist ties?!?). Anyway, recommended.

I was skeptical and thought these new razors might be the same sheep in a new set of wolf's clothing. When examining, it feels more fragile and probably should be handled with more care; especially when opening the cutters for the basic cleaning and rinsing which is now recommended to be done daily. Also, to charge the razor, it is more inconvenient. The charger plugs into the stand and cannot plug directly into the razor. Consequently, when traveling, the stand has to be packed along with the razor and charger. Before, just the razor and charger needed to be packed. As a consolation, there is a better (sturdier) travel case that is fairly compact, and it offers a littler more protection than the older style soft pouches.<br /><br />When turning it on, you will immediately notice a major difference. The motor sounds a lot different than the previous models. It sounds much weaker (less powerful) with a higher whiny pitch, almost like it is defective. Presumably, this is because the newer shaving blades do not need as much torque, and shave off more whiskers with less force.<br /><br />I have used it for one month (directions say 3 weeks are needed to get optimal results). Out of the box, the shave is definitely closer. My skin is smoother, and it cuts hairs in the challenging places the older model failed to shear (like the area just below the nose, lower neck, upper cheeks, clef chin crevasses, to name a few). It takes me longer to complete shaving , a 3rd to double the time but the results seem to be worth the effort. Before, a 3rd or 4th pass did nothing except irritate the skin. Now, the multiple passes crop the few parts that were missed. Also, the shaver does not irritate the skin (like the old one). I shave with my skin dry and do not use any creams.<br /><br />The battery gauge indicating how much charge time is left is not very helpful but this does not matter. Like the older models, it seems best to recharge it after half the charge is depleted. Also, the side-burn trimmer seems to be improved. It is narrower but trims better, reducing the need (but not eliminate) for regularly using an additional trimmer / groomer. The trimmer is is too awkward by its design next to the main shaving heads to use for fine detailing around eyebrows. It would be nice if they added a detail trimmer to the unit that works good for detailing eyebrows (and the hairs protruding from the ears and nose). (I suggest borrowing from the famous swiss army knifes and add a detail trimmer at the bottom so is could be used unencumbered by the big shaving heads.   725. I just switched from a DE razor (Merkur Classic, Israeli Personna blades) to electric, and bought both the Philips Norelco SensoTouch 3D 1250X and the Panasonic ES8243A. I've spent a few weeks with both, and here is what I found:<br /><br />First, the &#34;try it for 3 weeks&#34; thing is REAL. The first two weeks were terrible. Shaves were not close, I had irritation, redness and ingrown hairs. I tried shaving wet and dry, with similar results. Then, miraculously, halfway through Week 3, everything cleared up. Once that happened, the electric shaves were closer than my DE (or closer than I was willing to go with my DE).<br /><br />For background: my beard is fairly thick, and has a few regions that grow in different directions. The hair on my neck is all over the place. My hair is straight and black, my skin is brown and rather delicate, and I used to shave 2-3 times a week because it would take 15 minutes.<br /><br />Now, to compare:<br /><br />Closeness: both shavers are closer than doing a single with-the-grain pass of a DE razor. The Panasonic was noticeably (to the touch) closer on my face and chin, and the Norelco was possibly slightly closer on my jawline and neck. Both shavers also miss the same areas, creating consistently longer zones into two spots on my neck. My wife says she doesn't notice, but I do.<br /><br />Speed: average shave time with Panasonic was 4'15&#34;. Average shave time with Norelco was 5'30&#34;.<br /><br />Number of passes: on straight surfaces, the Panasonic needed just a few passes to cover the area. On curved areas, the Panasonic needed a lot of angling and back and forth, but it was a precise operation. The Norelco always needed a long random walk with lots and lots of passes, I think because the ratio of cutting surface to contact surface is much lower. The one exception is that flat-lying hairs would get picked up more quickly by the Norelco (though they wouldn't get cut as short).<br /><br />Comfort: both were very comfortable to shave with. After the 3-week adjustment, both caused no irritation or redness.<br /><br />Cleanup: easy on both. Though average cleanup time was about 0'40&#34; with the Panasonic, and 0'30&#34; with the Norelco.<br /><br />Coolness: The Norelco is SO COOL. It looks amazing, and feels like robot kisses when you shave with it. The Panasonic is not beautiful, and the Black/Orange display screams &#34;budget&#34;. The Norelco is a gadget, while the Panasonic is just a tool.<br /><br />Price: current pricing and coupons at the time I bought these put them pretty close together. $100 for the 1250X, and $85 for the 8243A.<br /><br />Overall: I love the Norelco so much. It is so, so cool. But it takes an extra minute, and is not quite as close. So I'm returning the Norelco and keeping the Panasonic. I have agonized over this decision way more than I intended, and I'm glad it's over. I also have to shout out to Philips customer service. Getting an RMA number was really easy and took less than 5 minutes.

  818. A little about me before I get into the shaver so you'll know where I'm coming from: I've been a Gillette razor guy for about 20 years. I've owned a few electric razors before, but only one \\"high end\\" electric; a Braun. The others were $10-$20 Remingtons or such that I would use when I traveled or when I was in the field when I was in the military. When I was in the military, I shaved 5x a week, but let my face \\"rest\\" on the weekends. Now I work 4 days a week, so I wouldn't shave on my days off. My facial hair grows rather quickly, so I would have about 3-4mm of growth after my days off. The first day I shaved, my face would be very smooth, but after day 2 or 3, I'd get razor bumps on my neck and some ingrown hairs. The razor bumps and ingrown hairs were probably caused by my desire to get as close a shave as the first day, so I would go against the grain. I received the Norelco as a XMas gift, so I waited to review it after my face had become accustomed to the razor.<br /><br />Shave quality: Very good. I shave in the shower with Edge shave gel. It's probably the closest I've ever had in my limited experience in using electric shavers. No, it's not \\"against the grain with a blade after a weekend of not shaving\\" close, but it's very, VERY good. It gets me near razor close on my cheeks and the left and right side of my neck, but there's still a little \\"sandpaper\\" feel when I run my hand against the grain underneath my jaw, down my Adam's apple, and some spots underneath my nose. Most importantly, I haven't experienced any bumps or ingrown hair since Ive started using the Norelco. Every now and then I'll feel some minor irritation, but it's nothing some Nivea after-shave balm won't cure.<br /><br />Shave time: Very good. I shower first and use a face wash, just like when I used a Gillette razor, so my beard is wet and softened by the hot water. I lather up the Edge gel and go in circular movements as the shaver's manual calls for. I'll alternate the circular pattern,so if I start with clockwise motions, I'll go back again but use counter-clockwise motions. I've read some reviews where they complained that it took more than one pass to get the shave as close as possible, to which I say; Duh!! To me, that's like buying a Prius for the gas mileage, then complaining that it doesn't have the towing capacity of your Ford F150. Yes, it takes a few passes to get all the hair, but it's not like you'll be spending an extra ten minutes shaving either.<br /><br />Battery life: Excellent. My girlfriend bought me the Sensotouch 3D for Xmas 2012. I let it fully charge and began using it around December 26. Today (Jan 20, 2013) was the first time I put it back on the charger, so I am very impressed with the battery life so far. MY shaver wasn't completely dead, but it was down to 1 bar of \\"life\\" and I'd used it two or three times after I'd noticed the battery was down to 1 bar. I figure I probably used it around 20 times, so a little better performance than the manufacturer's claim of 17 uses.<br /><br />Trimmer, cleaning, & Misc: The trimmer is just meh. I keep a Gillette Fusion next to my sink for trimming my sideburns because it has a single trimmer blade on the back and I find it gives my sideburns a perfect edge. I tried the Norelco's, but it's just not as good. If I had to grade it on a 1-5 scale, the trimmer would probably get a 2.<br /><br />Cleaning is very easy. Since I shave in the shower, I pop open the heads and run them under the shower. The owner's manual says you can also remove the heads for a more thorough cleaning, but I've found it's not a necessity. When I did the thorough cleaning, there wasn't any hair to be cleaned so I think rinsing it under hot water does well enough.<br /><br />I've seen a review where the person says he worries that if he drops it on the bathroom floor, the razor would break into \\"a million pieces\\". Again, I have to say; Duh! You don't drop valuable, semi-electronic instruments onto hard surfaces. Iknow some people are clumsy, but the shaver feels sturdy enough. I imagine if you're clumsy or careless, you should probably look for a different shaver, like one made of solid steel and titanium.<br /><br />Overall, I'm very happy with my Norelco 3D. I gave it 5 stars, though that might be a little generous, but I do think it's higher than 4. If Amazon had increments, I'd say the Norelco Sensotouch 3D is somewhere around 4.75 stars with the biggest knock being the trimmer. My shaver came with an extra shaver head, which Norelco recommends you replace every year. I think the 3D exceeds my expectations when it comes to shave quality and since I don't get any more bumps or ingrown hairs, I'm really enjoying the shaver. As with everything else in life, YMMV.
